Both games will take place at the Arena Ciudad de Mexico in Mexico City. As the big games approach, players from both teams (as well as some NBA legends) are getting ready for the event. The NBA Mexico City Games 2018 will mark the 27th and 28th games in Mexico since 1992, the most NBA games held in any country outside the United States and Canada. In 2017, the NBA played four games in Mexico, which marked the first time the league has held four regular-season games in one country outside the U.S. and Canada in one calendar year. Once the NBA Mexico City Games 2020 are done, the NBA will have played 32 games in Mexico since 1992. Irving finished with 38 points and seven assists and earned \u201cM-V-P\u201d chants late. He\u2019s one of the reasons the resurgent Celtics are on a seven-game winning streak. Wall, playing on a sore left heel, was no slouch. He poured in 34 points with 13 assists, an All-Star performance by most standards. Wall scored seven points in overtime, but was outdueled by Irving\u2019s 12. The Celtics\u2019 victory was impressive because they won on the road even though they were without Al Horford, Gordon Hayward and Jaylen Brown. Marcus Morris stepped up for Boston, scoring 27 and grabbing nine rebounds. * Thursday on NBA TV: Celtics vs. Wizards re-airs (4 p.m. ET) Anthony Davis put up a season-high 44 points and grabbed 18 boards, both highs among the night\u2019s top performers , as he helped the Pelicans hold off the Thunder, 118-114 . It was a dominant performance by Davis, who dunked seven times, but what sealed the victory was AD\u2019s rim-protecting presence on the defensive end. With the Thunder trailing 116-114 and fewer than 10 seconds remaining, Russell Westbrook had a lane to attack the basket for the tying bucket. But as Davis moved to guard the rim, Westbrook kicked the ball out to Alex Abrines, whose 3-point attempt banged off the front iron. The Pelicans secured the rebound for the win. Davis\u2019 night overshadowed Paul George, who had an All-Star night with 25 points, 11 boards and five assists. The much-anticipated showdown between the league-leading Raptors and the defending champion Warriors failed to live up to expectations. Playing the second of a back-to-back without Kawhi Leonard (sore right hip), the still-energetic Raptors took an early lead and kept it, routing the champs 113-93 . It was the first win in Oracle Arena for the Raptors since Feb. 8, 2004. The only negative for Toronto was the loss of Jonas Valanciunas with a dislocated left thumb in the first quarter. Kyle Lowry, who appears to be coming out of his shooting slump, logged 23 points and 12 assists for the Raptors. Kevin Durant led the Warriors with 30 points. Stephen Curry had an uncharacteristic shooting night, going 3-for-12 from the floor and 2-for-8 from 3-point range. Jeremy Lamb\u2019s tough bucket with a defender in his grill lifted the Charlotte Hornets to a 108-107 win over the Detroit Pistons. It wasn\u2019t a buzzer-beater, but the 22-footer from the right wing came close, with 0.03 of a second left. Lamb finished with 13 points, overshadowing another stellar night from Kemba Walker, who posted a near triple-double with 31 points, eight rebounds and nine assists. Blake Griffin had 26 points and 10 rebounds for the Pistons in a losing effort. After a relatively strong start to the season, skidding Detroit has lost six in a row. Scrappy guard and fan favorite Matthew Dellavedova enjoyed a warm reception in his first game back in Cleveland as a Cavalier. The Aussie proceeded to nail a 3-pointer, and he moved past 2,000 points in his six-season NBA career. Dellavedova contributed big off the bench in the Cavaliers\u2019 113-106 win over the Knicks, scoring 15 points in 22 minutes, including shooting 3-for-5 from beyond the arc. This earned him a playful \u201cM-V-P\u201d chant. Rookies Luka Doncic and Trae Young, who were traded for each other on Draft night, had almost identical stat lines Wednesday night. But Doncic and the Mavericks earned the victory over Young and the Hawks , 114-107. Young finished with 24 points and 10 assists in 35 minutes, while Doncic had 24 points, 10 rebounds and six assists. The Mavericks\u2019 win was the first over the Hawks since Oct. 30, 2013. Draymond Green is back. Are we about to see the Warriors pull away from the pack in the crowded Western Conference?  * * * Steve Aschburner :  Not only that, but DeMarcus Cousins is on his way back too. I do think Golden State has both the ability and the motivation now to put some distance between itself and the challengers of the West. Old nemesis Houston isn\u2019t pushing hard from behind, but OKC and Denver are hungry, high-quality teams that the Warriors dare not take lightly. Plus coach Steve Kerr always is looking for a new edge with which to play the regular season. And there\u2019s this: Golden State should want to leave the fans who have made Oracle Arena such a fantastic home court with something special. Playoff schedules are unpredictable, but the Warriors know what home games they have remaining in the regular season and ought to show off their best selves the rest of the way. Shaun Powell :   Yes, yes, yes. Not just because the Warriors are stocked better than anyone else, but there isn\u2019t a strong No. 2 in the West, not like last season. My hunch is the Christmas Day game with the Los Angeles Lakers will determine first place in the West, and that\u2019s the springboard the Warriors will use to leap beyond everyone else. That overblown KD-Draymond dustup (happens on plenty of teams) is history. Draymond\u2019s back, Steph\u2019s back and DeMarcus Cousins is coming. John Schuhmann :  All the ingredients are there. Denver is banged up, with Gary Harris and Paul Millsap both out for a few weeks. The next few weeks of Oklahoma City\u2019s schedule are tougher than the last few weeks were, and the LA Clippers have been showing signs of slippage. When the Warriors are healthy, they can be the league\u2019s best team on both ends of the floor and put together a lot of wins. But the champs are about to begin a tough stretch of the schedule themselves. Eight of their next nine games are against teams with winning records, and the only exception is a game in Utah (where the Warriors lost two games by a total of 70 points last season ). They can obviously beat any team in the league, six of those other eight games are at home, and they just finished a five-game trip with an impressive win in Milwaukee. But these next 18 days will tell us a lot about where they\u2019re at in regard to their focus on both ends of the floor. For the sake of assistant coach Ron Adams\u2019 sanity, it would be nice to see them climb from 17th to the top 10 in defensive efficiency by the end of the month. Sekou Smith :  We are absolutely going to see the Warriors stretch out in the coming weeks. They\u2019ve been waiting all season to get healthy enough to play to their true form. Add in the fact DeMarcus Cousins is clearly ramping up for his debut and the rest of the West should brace themselves for the flurry. They\u2019ll use all of these early-season hiccups as reminders of how quickly things can go awry when they\u2019re not on their grind. It might be the one thing they really needed to focus themselves prior to the start of the postseason. Talent-wise we know they don\u2019t have a peer in the Western Conference or the league. What\u2019s one thing \u2014 the first thing \u2014 this franchise needs to do to get back on track?  * * * Steve Aschburner :  Stick to the Xs and Os for a while, and do it according to generally accepted activity principles. That means new coach Jim Boylen conveying the necessary messages in 90-minute practices and 45-minute shootarounds and backing off from the way he overloaded the work schedule in his first week. It also means the players focusing \u2014 hard \u2014 on basketball and behaving just a teeny, tiny bit like what they\u2019re doing is a job, with accountability and bosses\u2019 demands. It was a miserable look to complain about a practice the day after participating, at home, in the franchise\u2019s most lopsided loss ever, regardless of the five previous days\u2019 duties. Presumably both sides have grown from the embarrassing episode, and the healthiest Bulls squad so far this season can get busy doubling its victory total in, say, half the 28 games it took just to get six. Shaun Powell :   They need to take a serious look at the front office and see if it\u2019s working. Gar Foreman and John Paxson have had some decent drafts but little else and it\u2019s apparent they have a coaching problem here in December. For a team that hasn\u2019t put forth a reliable foundation, that from office has remained in place for a long time. Might be time to go in another direction. John Schuhmann :  More often than not, success and failure in this league start at the top. Bulls\u2019 ownership and the front office team of Gar Forman and John Paxson need to look in the mirror and figure out why the organization isn\u2019t functioning the right way. Even when the team was having success (the Tom Thibodeau years), there was a disconnect between management and the coaching staff. I\u2019m not sure how they go from where they are now to having everyone pulling in the same direction, but it is possible to hire a coach that\u2019s neither too tough nor too soft on the players. The development of their two young big men \u2014 Lauri Markkanen and Wendell Carter Jr. \u2014 within a constructive environment should be priority No. 1. Sekou Smith :  The first thing the Bulls have to do is decide who is going to serve as the leader of the franchise. And not in name or in theory, but in the flesh. Whoever that is (owner or front-office man), he better step up and fill that void immediately. And if that\u2019s not the coach, fine. But if the players in that locker room are left to wonder who is the true leader of that operation, it\u2019s an issue that will continue to drag the entire group down. That\u2019s why I\u2019m never in favor of in-season coaching changes without a clear-cut vision of who the replacement is and that replacement being given every resource to do the job right. The Chicago Bulls and coach Jim Boylen need to focus on the tangibles of what\u2019s left of this season or risk losing something worse than an unseemly number of basketball games. They risk losing their reputations. The Bulls were mired in intangibles for more than a week, and it went horribly. When the Bulls fired Fred Hoiberg on Dec. 3, VP of basketball operations John Paxson cited an absence of \u201cpassion,\u201d \u201cenergy\u201d and \u201cspirit\u201d as the overriding \u2014 yet intangible \u2014 reasons. Urgent ones, too, because the Bulls didn\u2019t even wait to give Hoiberg a chance to work with a semblance of a full roster. Stretch big Lauri Markkanen played his first game just two days before the firing. Point guard Kris Dunn (strained left knee) and forward Bobby Portis (strained right knee), returned Monday night against the Sacramento Kings. Boylen revved up and muscled up with a little training-camp-in-December. He reportedly ran practices that lasted well over two hours \u2014 once, twice, three times in the first four days. He hit the Bulls with a heavy dose of conditioning work, with suicide sprints and military-style push-ups. He ordered film breakdowns immediately after Chicago\u2019s loss to the Indiana Pacers on Dec. 4 . A two-point upset of Oklahoma City on Friday was followed Saturday by the worst defeat in Bulls history . The 133-77 pasting by the Boston Celtics was humiliating, from the 17-0 hole the Bulls dug themselves to Boylen theatrically subbing out all the starters not once, but twice. Yet that performance wasn\u2019t even the most embarrassing thing the Bulls did last weekend. That came Sunday, when players reportedly considered boycotting Boylen\u2019s scheduled practice. A couple of them initiated a group text late Saturday to muster support for the resistance \u2014 they thought it was \u201cexcessive,\u201d Boylen later told reporters, to practice after a back-to-back and on the lone slack day in a stretch of three games in four nights. (Both are contrary to common NBA work schedules). They allegedly even contacted the National Basketball Players Association to see if union rules were being violated (they were not). \u201cThis is not a negotiation,\u201d Boylen said. The ringleaders were described in some Chicago media reports as \u201cveterans,\u201d which narrows the list of suspects quickly \u2014 only four Bulls players have as much as four years of NBA experience. Robin Lopez, 30, specifically was mentioned as a vet who slowed the resisters\u2019 roll, telling them how unprofessional they\u2019d be perceived. So, per one team source, the players\u2019 big stand wound up as walking in at 12:15 p.m. instead of the scheduled noon practice time. They did avoid another potential killer workout by instead heading into a players-only meeting, followed by a players-coaches-management meeting after. Then some players got some shots up while a handful played 2-on-2. Per ESPN\u2019s Malika Andrews and Ramona Shelburne on Tuesday, after the players-coaches-management meeting, the idea of forming a leadership committee was discussed . The idea there was that in the future, those appointed to the leadership committee could act as a liason between players and coaches. ESPN also reports that Bulls management is on board with Boylen\u2019s tough-love leadership style and are supporting him as he uses a firm hand to change the team\u2019s culture. All that said, the Bulls spit out the bit against the Kings at United Center Monday. They were outscored 63-33 in the second half and got booed at the end. Again. Hopefully, that now is that. This has been way too much drama for a 6-22 team ill-equipped to handle it at either the coaching or playing level. Boylen got into the weeds of the intangibles that got him promoted. He was dwelling on basketball\u2019s last refuge of scoundrels, hustle factors, because that\u2019s what his bosses apparently value most, as evidenced by their dismissal of Hoiberg. Pushing the players as hard as he did in his first seven days \u2014 and talking enthusiastically about it to the media \u2014 led invariably to players pushing back. They were wrong for doing so \u2014 the leaders on better, more veteran teams would have demanded a practice Sunday after Chicago\u2019s loss. But many of these Bulls players are too young, too inexperienced and too of-their-generation to realize how wrong they were. There was no way anything resembling NBA basketball (never mind the winning variety) could have continued, as raw as things got in the 48 hours or so before Monday\u2019s loss. Now, in the hangover from raw emotions and a pair of regrettable defeats, Boylen can busy himself with the fine points of cleaning up the Bulls\u2019 defense, turnover woes and defense on 3-pointers and side pick-and-rolls. They all can use the itinerary quirk of a brief trip to Mexico City for Thursday\u2019s Global Game against Orlando ( 9:30 p.m. ET, NBA League Pass ), followed by games at San Antonio and OKC, to do some familiar road bonding. Even the stop to face the Spurs can help, provided it gets Boylen to back off some of his Gregg Popovich references in the presence of the real deal (and the Bulls players stop feeling compelled to remind their coach he\u2019s not Pop). If not quite tranquil, there seemed to be a calming down \u2014 maybe a playing out \u2014 by late Monday. \u201cGood, bad or ugly, I think that ordeal was good for the team,\u201d Bulls guard Zach LaVine said. Said Boylen: \u201cI think it\u2019s a blessing for where we want to go.\u201d Maybe. But like the coach said when asked how a team digs out from such an emotional hole, the Bulls are going to be in \u201cwin the next possession\u201d mode for some time. This group has built no track record and has nothing to lean on, besides some talent. Oh, and all the new passion, energy and spirit. The Bulls and Boylen are stuck with each other, and they won\u2019t become any other team\u2019s nemeses until they stop being each other\u2019s worst enemies. * * * Steve Aschburner has written about the NBA since 1980. Abdur-Rahim will replace Malcolm Turner, who will step down Jan. 11, 2019, to become the Athletics Director at Vanderbilt University. In his new role, Abdur-Rahim will be responsible for all aspects of the NBA G League\u2019s business and basketball operations, including the implementation of the newly formed professional path, ongoing testing of experimental rules and league-wide expansion efforts.  \u201cShareef\u2019s unique experiences as a player, team executive and member of the NBA\u2019s Basketball Operations department make him a fantastic fit to be the next President of the NBA G League,\u201d said Tatum. \u201cHe is well-prepared to build on the tremendous progress that the NBA G League has made under Malcolm, who deftly oversaw a pivotal period of expansion and transition. We thank Malcolm for his lasting contributions to the NBA and the NBA G League and wish him the best at Vanderbilt.\u201d  Abdur-Rahim, who turned 42 today, previously worked five years with the Sacramento Kings, serving as an assistant general manager and assistant coach as well as spending the 2013-14 season as general manager of the NBA G League\u2019s Reno Bighorns (now known as the Stockton Kings). Abdur-Rahim earned a bachelor\u2019s degree from the University of California at Berkeley and an MBA from the University of Southern California Marshall School of Business. As a player, Abdur-Rahim averaged 18.1 points per game in 12 NBA seasons. The third overall pick in the 1996 NBA Draft, he was named an NBA All-Star with the Atlanta Hawks in the 2001-02 season. Abdur-Rahim also earned a gold medal with USA Basketball at the 2000 Sydney Olympics. \u201cI am thrilled to have this extraordinary opportunity with the NBA G League,\u201d said Abdur-Rahim. \u201cI\u2019ve seen firsthand the NBA G League\u2019s remarkable growth under Malcolm\u2019s leadership, and I look forward to working with the players, teams and my colleagues to take the league to even greater heights.\u201d  \u201cI feel very fortunate to have had the chance to lead the NBA G League,\u201d said Turner. \u201cI am proud of the transformational work we have done toward achieving our goal of a 30-team league. I want to thank the NBA G League\u2019s owners, presidents, coaches and team staffs for their partnership and Adam Silver and Mark Tatum for their guidance and for entrusting this important part of the NBA\u2019s business to me.\u201d During Turner\u2019s four-year tenure, the NBA G League expanded by 10 teams (from 18 during the 2014-15 season to 28 for the 2019-20 season) and transitioned from the NBA Development League to the NBA G League as part of a first-of-its-kind entitlement partnership with Gatorade. Additionally, Turner\u2019s commitment to increased developmental opportunities paved the way for the implementation of both NBA Two-Way and Select Contracts.  Under Turner\u2019s leadership, the NBA G League\u2019s impact on the NBA game has skyrocketed. When he joined the NBA G League in October 2014, 33 percent of players on 2013-14 NBA end-of-season rosters had NBA G League experience. Four years later, that number grew to 53 percent to close the 2017-18 season. Additionally, Turner orchestrated an enhanced partnership with USA Basketball to field teams comprised of NBA G League players during the qualifying rounds of the 2019 FIBA Basketball World Cup.  The NBA G League set records for attendance and visibility last season as more than 1.6 million fans attended games (an increase of more than 11 percent over the previous season) and combined viewership across ESPNU and NBA TV grew five percent from 2016-17 to 2017-18. Additionally, the league shattered records for social media metrics last season, with more than 150 million video views and four million actions \u2013 increases of 47 percent and 25 percent, respectively.  About the NBA G League The NBA\u2019s official minor league, the NBA G League prepares players, coaches, officials, trainers and front-office staff for the NBA while acting as the league\u2019s research and development laboratory. Featuring 27 teams with direct affiliations with NBA franchises for the 2018-19 season, the league offers elite professional basketball at an affordable price in a fun, family-friendly atmosphere. An all-time-high 53 percent of all NBA players at the end of the 2017-18 season boasted NBA G League experience. In fostering the league\u2019s connection to the community, its teams, players and staff promote health and wellness, support local needs and interests, and assist in educational development through NBA Cares programs. "},{"id":36989,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/kiki-vandeweghe-qa-highest-scoring-game-ever","date":"2018-12-10","title":"Q&A: Magical night in '83 still vivid for VanDeWeghe","content":" Three or four NBA coaches were yukking it up during a lull in their annual September meetings in Chicago, familiar rivals renewing old and building new friendships. At one point, a familiar figure \u2014 tall, bespectacled, in an all-business suit \u2014 headed their way on the hotel\u2019s banquet-hall level. The coach who spotted Kiki VanDeWeghe first quickly alerted his peers. \u201cShhh. Shhh! SHHH!\u201d that fellow said in a stage whisper. \u201cIt\u2019s the PO-lice!\u201d The others turned, saw VanDeWeghe and laughed heartily, as the NBA\u2019s executive vice president, basketball operations, smiled and joined them. It would seem a tricky and potentially awkward thing, being the one who can suspend players and whack coaches\u2019 wallets. But VanDeWeghe handles the duty without much stress on either side and has been doing so since 2013 .  VanDeWeghe, 60, has worked as many jobs, at as many levels, as arguably anyone in NBA history. He logged 13 seasons with the Denver Nuggets, Portland Trail Blazers, New York Knicks and LA Clippers, averaging 19.7 points on 52.5 percent shooting while making two All-Star teams. In the 25 years since he retired, VanDeWeghe has served as general manager with Denver and New Jersey, with one season as interim coach of the Nets. He worked as a broadcast analyst for two years with ESPN and spent two years with FOX Sports West covering the Clippers. He joined the league office in April 2013 and was promoted into his current position later that year. Beyond meting out fines and suspensions, VanDeWeghe has responsibilities with the Competition Committee, game analytics and game operations, while serving as a liaison between the NBA and its teams. He also holds the distinction of being the top scorer in the highest-scoring game in NBA history . Detroit beat Denver in triple-overtime, 186-184, at McNichols Sports Arena on Dec. 13, 1983 and VanDeWeghe finished with 51 points, nine rebounds and eight assists . With the 35th anniversary of that milestone game fast approaching, VanDeWeghe spoke with NBA.com\u2019s Steve Aschburner about the game, the frantic scoring pace that the league seems to be embracing and more: * * * Steve Aschburner:  Three hundred seventy points \u2014 and 80 of them came after the fourth quarter. What stands out for you from that crazy game? Kiki VanDeWeghe b At the time, it was kind of a surreal event. It felt like this game went on forever. The number of overtimes, lots of heroic plays, so there was just tons of drama throughout the game. The Pistons were a tough team. On some level, it was the beginnings of the Bad Boys era. They hadn\u2019t added everybody yet, but they had a core group there \u2014 Isiah Thomas was so tough and [Bill] Laimbeer was Laimbeer, and Vinnie Johnson was the Microwave. SA:  Did you and the others realize you were making history?  KV:  What I remember is how tired everybody was, and how after that game, it was like, \u201cOh man!\u201d Even for a couple of games after that, our team felt it. It was one of those things where you know you\u2019re going through something unique and that it probably won\u2019t happen again, and you\u2019re tired but you\u2019re fired up to experience it. I don\u2019t know if you think you\u2019re making history, but in some small way you get that perspective. At least I did. And it\u2019s sort of exciting \u2013 it\u2019s what you play basketball for, that type of competition. SA:  The astounding thing to me is, four years into the 3-pointer\u2019s NBA existence, each team was 1-of-2 from the arc. Makes me think Golden State and Houston conceivably could top 200 points each. KV:  The pace of that game was right at 112. Currently, we\u2019re just north of 110. So we\u2019re playing at that speed, and the thing we\u2019ve added is 3-pointers. That\u2019s what clearly stands out to me about the box score. SA:  So maybe your two teams could have topped 200, with 63 minutes to work with.  KV:  It did seem like that. Believe me. SA:  By all rights, a team that misses 23 free throws \u2014 Detroit shot 37-of-60 from the foul line \u2014 ought to lose the game. What was it like for your team to score 184 and lose? KV:  It was deflating, I\u2019m not going to lie to you. That was a very tough loss. I thought we had it won in regulation, I thought we had it won a number of times. It\u2019s just a truism of the NBA that if you let a team hang around long enough, they\u2019re going to have a run and you run the risk of losing that game. SA:  Do you remember the points or basket that won it? KV:  What I remember is Isiah Thomas did a lot at the end to win. That didn\u2019t surprise me. He was such a great competitor. If I recall, we were No. 1 in scoring [that season] and it really was a contrast in styles. Detroit was coached a certain way, we were coached a certain way. We scored 184 points and never ran a play. We played a passing game and the only rule [coach] Doug Moe had was, you couldn\u2019t stand [still]. You had to go do something. Well, we did have two out-of-bounds plays, as I remember it. Alex English went 1-on-1 or I went 1-on-1. Those were our two out-of-bounds plays. SA:  You were putting up Hall of Fame scoring and shooting numbers in those days. KV:  Early in my career I was much more of a driver. But later in that year, I hurt my back for the first time. The next year, I hurt it twice, and after that, I couldn\u2019t really jump well. The medical side was so different. Now there is such a focus on health and wellness, and teams are so advanced on rest, rehab, how to get the body back in shape. Techniques are so much better. I think about it all the time \u2013 if we had had that type of focus and advances in treatment. Because I never really got [healthy]. I turned into a jump shooter. I played a long time after that but wasn\u2019t quite the same player. SA:  Four weeks after the 186-184 game, your Nuggets team beat San Antonio in regulation, 163-155. You scored 50 that night. Did that soothe some of the sting? KV:  No. I remember this game. Athletes, they remember the losses and the missed shots, the game-winners that could have been. Those are the things that still haunt you. SA:  So do you think we\u2019ll see that record \u2013370 points, two teams \u2014 broken? KV:  I\u2019m going to say yes. For years I said \u201cNo, that\u2019ll last forever.\u201d But if you look at the average pace the NBA plays at today, if you look at 3-pointers, if you look at shooting at a high level, I do think one of these nights you\u2019re going to see high two high-scoring teams go a couple of overtimes and do it. SA:  No problem with losing a claim to fame? KV:  Look, we remember things fondly and tend to get better with age. But I can tell you honestly, the game has never been better. We\u2019ve never had more stars. We\u2019ve never had better talent. Skill sets. Shooters in our game. Just across the board, the creativity. Like you, I watch a lot of games. And I\u2019m surprised, I\u2019m stunned, I rewind wondering, \u201cDid I see what I just saw?\u201d In many ways, it\u2019s more exciting today. You\u2019ve got the tremendous pace, you\u2019ve got 3-point shots, you\u2019ve got incredible athleticism. SA:  So about your current gig \u2013 is it awkward for you being in charge of players\u2019 and coaches\u2019 discipline? KV:  Most of these guys are really good friends of mine for a very long time. The important thing is communication. Making sure coaches, teams, know what direction we\u2019re headed. We\u2019re very transparent in what we share with the referees. We keep in constant contact with the general managers and coaches. It\u2019s a real sharing of ideas. Obviously people want to win games and they fight for their teams, but when we get together as a group, it\u2019s about the good of the game. These are basketball people, and they want to make the game better.  SA:  Sounds like a legit two-way street, rather than top down. KV:  They\u2019re on the front lines, and we tend to listen. Quite honestly, that\u2019s where most of our rule changes come from. Let\u2019s be honest, this is a little bit of a complaint department \u2014 teams call me all the time \u2014 and the most frequent complaint we got [last season] was away from the ball, freedom of movement, and how to keep the game moving. And the post play, with all the switching that\u2019s going on, that\u2019s gotten a little rough. That\u2019s typically how we get a Competition Committee agenda \u2014 it comes from our teams. SA:  As far as discipline, it seems the league \u2014 with the possible exception of visiting locker-room intrusions at Staples Center \u2014 has built up enough precedent that the parties involved almost know what\u2019s coming, in fines or suspensions. Does that make things go down more smoothly? KV:  We have a clear system for how we deal with things consistently, the same way every time. It helps to have people weigh in. We look at history. We look at comparables and context that matters. We spend a lot of time talking to everybody involved in incidents. We really try to get an idea of what truly happened. I\u2019m proud of where we end up in most cases. And the idea is, it\u2019s much less about punishment than it is about deterring behavior, and making sure players can compete and show their natural abilities. And be safe on the court. SA:  Does the NBA keep an eye on the NFL, NHL or MLB when it comes to discipline and policies, or are things too cooked into the respective collective bargaining agreements to have much crossover value? KV:  We do look at them. It\u2019s different for each league, different rules, and not all of it\u2019s applicable. But we do try to incorporate many times \u201cbest practices\u201d \u2014 if there\u2019s something we see another league doing, and we think \u201cthat\u2019s a really good idea,\u201d we\u2019ll adopt it. That\u2019s one thing [NBA commissioner] Adam [Silver] has been so focused on \u2014 keeping us improving. \u201cHey, don\u2019t be satisfied that you\u2019re doing a good job and everybody seems to be happy. Do better.\u201d That\u2019s a big mantra. And not only [borrowing] from the other leagues but from other businesses. SA:  Your predecessor in this job, Rod Thorn, went into the Hall of Fame this year. Did he give you any advice as you took the job? KV:  Rod was a great relationship guy and still I view him as somebody who\u2019s a mentor and advisor. Rod said, \u201cAt the end, be tough. But make sure you leave \u2018em laughing.\u201d * * * Steve Aschburner has written about the NBA since 1980. You can e-mail him here , find his archive here and follow him on Twitter . The Warriors join the 1980 U.S. hockey team, the 1999 U.S. Women\u2019s World Cup soccer squad and the 2004 Boston Red Sox as the other team honorees. They\u2019re really a generational team. I don\u2019t know if, in my lifetime, there has been a team where the pieces have blended so beautifully together.\u201d Stone also said that the Warriors\u2019 honor is more about the celebration of the organization doing something unique over an extended period while the other teams were honored for what they did in a certain year. Though he says he doesn\u2019t care, the fifth-year veteran continues to make his case, delivering another impressive performance in what is shaping up to be his breakout season. With All-Star centerpiece Anthony Davis hampered by a hip injury, Randle picked up the slack with 28 points, six rebounds and five assists as the Pelicans defeated the Pistons 116-108 for just their fourth road win of the season. It marked Randle\u2019s fourth straight game with at least 26 points \u2014 you guessed it, all starts in replacement of the injured Nikola Mirotic. Randle is averaging 29.5 points and 11.3 rebounds over that span with a plus 17.8 net rating. Along the way he set career highs in scoring (37 points, against the Clippers) and rebounds (18, against the Mavericks) in back-to-back games. It continued Randle\u2019s trend of performing significantly better as a starter, averaging 24.8 points and 11.3 rebounds in those eight games compared to 17.0 points and 8.6 rebounds in 20 games off the bench. While he obviously gets more minutes as a starter, Randle also shoots roughly three percentage points better from the floor in that capacity. Pelicans coach Alvin Gentry has said he doesn\u2019t see himself making a definitive decision between Randle and Mirotic, preferring to choose depending on that night\u2019s matchup. But if Randle keeps tearing it up like a young Karl Malone, Gentry might not have a choice. On the other end of the heat index is Raptors point guard Kyle Lowry, whose recent stretch of frigid play reached its lowest point yet against the Bucks with one of the worst games of his career. Lowry finished without a single point for the first time since March 2013 and only the third start of his career. It marked his fourth straight game in single digits, and continued a stretch in which he\u2019s averaging a paltry 5.0 points on 19-percent shooting in more than 35 minutes over the past five games. Not surprisingly, the Raptors have dropped three of those contests, including 104-99 to the Bucks in a game where even a mediocre effort from their All-Star point guard might have made the difference. Lowry shot 0 for 5 against Milwaukee, all from 3-point range, and has taken 32 of his past 42 shots from beyond the arc. \u201cI don\u2019t know, I just couldn\u2019t find the open ones tonight,\u201d said Lowry, as quoted by the Toronto Star . \u201cI\u2019ve got to be a little bit more (aggressive) inside the paint, inside the arc. I definitely do.\u201d Replacing a coach midseason is never easy, but Jim Boylen has had an especially tough time taking over for the recently-sacked Fred Hoiberg in Chicago. After a six-point loss to the Pacers and a two-point win over the Thunder to start his tenure, Boylen saw his team get absolutely mauled by the Celtics on Saturday, losing by 56 points to set the Bulls record for largest defeat in team history and tie the NBA mark for worst home loss. Then came news that the players reportedly usurped his plans for a Sunday practice in order to hold a two-hour, players-only meeting, followed by an additional meeting with the coaching staff. As reported by ESPN , Boylen acknowledged after that gathering that there\u2019s been \u201ca little shock and awe\u201d in response to his aggressive approach, which has included lengthy benchings, tough practices and zero hesitation to criticize his team\u2019s effort, or lack thereof. (A handful of players were reportedly so unhappy with the prospect of another long workout on Sunday after games on Friday and Saturday \u2014 a rarity in the NBA \u2014 that they had to be talked into showing up at all.) Boylen\u2019s aggressive approach stands in stark contrast to the mild-mannered Hoiberg, who was fired last week with a 115-155 record and one playoff appearance in three-plus seasons. \u201cWe\u2019re still learning about each other,\u201d Boylen said. \u201cThey\u2019re still learning how I want it \u2026 and there\u2019s an adjustment to that.\u201d Said Zach LaVine, per the Chicago Tribune : \u201cWe needed to get a lot of stuff off our chest and be transparent. I don\u2019t think the players\u2019 toughness should ever be questioned. I think that\u2019s on us. "},{"id":37029,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/dwyane-wade-lebron-james-friendship","date":"2018-12-09","title":"Longtime friends James, Wade prepare for final meeting as opponents","content":" * On NBA TV:  Heat vs. Lakers (10:30 ET) LOS ANGELES \u2014  Friendships are never formed totally by choice, because fate demands a say-so in the process by creating the time and the place and in the curious case of LeBron James and Dwyane Wade, the basketball court. It was in Chicago, June of 2003, site of the NBA\u2019s annual Draft combine, the meet market for young players gathered to someday change the game, when Wade and LeBron had each other at wassup. In some ways, it was an unlikely pairing. One, a teenaged phenom from Akron, Ohio, fresh from the cover of Sports Illustrated and the high school prom who already had a national following. The other, an overlooked underdog from the Chicago suburbs who only became an acquired basketball taste weeks earlier after a searing run through the NCAA Tournament. That day, Wade and LeBron went through the checkup lines for height and weight, vertical leap and whatever else the combines put rookies through and then during a break came the only measurement that counted, when one future Hall of Famer sized up the other. LeBron said: \u201cSome things you can\u2019t explain. Sometimes it\u2019s just chemistry.\u201d Wade said: \u201cWhen you\u2019re young and coming into the league, you find guys you have something in common with, then you continue to link and that\u2019s what we did. It\u2019s organic how we built this friendship.\u201d Some 15 years later, the bond will endure, likely forever. The basketball part, however, ends Monday night after the game when Wade, who\u2019s calling it a career after this season, peels off his sweat-soaked Heat jersey and swaps it for a Laker top belonging to LeBron. It might qualify as the best trade of the NBA season, or at least the most emotional.  \u201cIt\u2019s sweet and sour,\u201d said LeBron, anticipating the moment at Staples Center. \u201cThe sweet part about it is I\u2019ve always loved being on the same floor with my brother. And the sour part about it is that this is our last time sharing the same court.\u201d Brother? How many folks with different blood can call each other that? True friendship is answering the phone at 3 a.m. instead of letting it ring, and reaching for the tab with longer arms, and above all, becoming a mattress when the other guy falls. Those tests were aced throughout the LeBron-Wade bromance that stretched through two Olympic teams, four years in Miami, two NBA championships and even 46 games in Cleveland together but of course was always put on hold whenever they were on opposite benches. This is best placed into proper context by Gabrielle Union, the actress and wife of Wade, who says ever so delicately about her husband in those friend vs. friend moments: \u201cHe wants to kill him. Drop three-balls on him.\u201d Perhaps so, because as Wade says, \u201cyou always want to beat your best friend,\u201d yet their competitive spirit is confined within the baselines and between the jump ball and buzzer. Then the teasing and bragging rights begin by text or call, almost instantly. This arrangement irked the old-school basketball culture, long cringing at the chummy ways of a new generation, believing that most if not all interaction should cease until the offseason, or even better, when careers are done. Wade and LeBron then turned up the volume on that subject when they linked up as teammates with the Heat in 2010, angering the purists and creating, at least initially, a team to be despised as well as respected. Not that Wade and LeBron regret that experience at all, or the noise that followed; this was, as Union observed, \u201cfar bigger than basketball.\u201d The chance to be neighbors and watch their kids grow up together and celebrate championships on South Beach until well past sunrise was a priceless part of the bonding process, something neither will be able to duplicate as they begin a new phase of their relationship. The chance to let their hair down (well, Wade anyway) and loosen up, away from the crowds and the media, is something they could keep to themselves. Although: Mrs. Wade spilled a few friendship secrets the other day, with an ohmigod and a roll of the eyes. \u201cThey laugh a lot,\u201d she said. \u201cLeBron is silly. Dwyane is silly. They\u2019re silly and goofy together. When they\u2019re around each other it\u2019s like a never-ending sleepover. That\u2019s what it feels like when you\u2019re in their orbit. They have an unspoken language and jokes and it\u2019s like a show and everyone\u2019s watching.\u201d It helped that, in addition to being in the same sport, both LeBron and Wade became all-time greats, because like-minded and like-talented people tend to magnetize. It was LeBron who collected MVP awards and a huge social media flock at first, then Wade followed up by winning a championship first, and this created a mutual respect for each other\u2019s abilities. It also allowed them to walk through the same exclusive doors together, for example, making a pair of Olympic teams and a batch of All-Star Games, therefore putting them in close company even before the Heat experience. From those moments, a relationship tightened. And when life threw airballs in their direction, one was there to help the other. \u201cWhen I was going through the custody of my kids and that battle, he was someone I talked to constantly and told him what I was going through,\u201d said Wade. \u201cAnd vice versa, when he was going through things family-wise, I could talk to him and try to relate. You lean on guys who have similar stories and have gone through similar things in their lives to help with advice or just be there to listen.\u201d Curiously, one of their few awkward moments happened when they became teammates in Miami initially. The transition, Wade admitted, was friction-free but not totally smooth. Superstars have egos. Adjustments were needed and were done and this was made possible by LeBron\u2019s game, which is built on unselfish play. \u201cIt would\u2019ve been easier if we went to a neutral site,\u201d Wade said. \u201cBut because he came to Miami, it was my team before he got there. It was a little hard because of that, but once we got through the first year it was easy. He can play with anybody. He can go out and score or he can get 17 points and 20 assists. He knows if a guy hasn\u2019t shot the ball in a while and how to get him going.\u201d Their on-court chemistry was astonishing to witness at times, the best entertainment in basketball back then. They knew each other\u2019s tendencies, spots on the floor and how to mesh. How many times did Wade toss a lob to a streaking LeBron for a dunk, or vice-versa? Along with Chris Bosh, this was one of the most productive link-ups in NBA history. Four years and four trips to the NBA Finals don\u2019t lie. And true friendship is following your pal to Cleveland in winter, as Wade did last year in an awkward attempt to re-create the past. To this, Wade shook his head and laughed: \u201cYeah, yeah, you right about that.\u201d While Wade is putting a bow on this retirement season, he marvels at his friend\u2019s staying power and salutes LeBron\u2019s decision to sign up with the Lakers and take on Los Angeles. \u201cI think it\u2019s great, something he wanted to do,\u201d Wade said. \u201cFor a player to be able to map out his career the way he has been able to do, he\u2019s doing it his way. This is the way he wanted, to end it here in L.A., on and off the court. His career is not over, but this is the last layer of his career.\u201d And LeBron, reflecting on Wade\u2019s NBA imprint, said: \u201cD-Wade has definitely had a helluva career, obviously. A first-ballot Hall of Famer, a three-time champion and so on and so on. I mean, it speaks for itself. But what he\u2019s done for that franchise and what he\u2019s done for that community since he\u2019s been drafted has been a pretty good story.\u201d This is curious timing, how the NBA schedule has Wade making his last trip to Los Angeles and against LeBron not long after Wade and Union, who have a home in L.A., recently welcomed a newborn daughter. The families spent Sunday together at the baby shower, then the farewell game tips 24 hours later. Union calls it the \u201cend of a basketball brotherhood but the beginning of a real friendship with basketball gone\u201d and Wade agrees. \u201cWhen we first came into the league people couldn\u2019t understand how we could be friends during the season,\u201d Wade said. \u201cWhen I was in Cleveland for a game I\u2019d go to his house the night before, we\u2019d go to the movies and hang out and then we\u2019d go at each other in the game. We\u2019d laugh about that. We enjoy having a different relationship than what was done before us, but then going out and playing against him, I\u2019d always want to whup his you-know-what. And vice versa. Just the times we shared. The moments when it\u2019s not all been great, but to be able to have somebody to talk to and run things by. A lot of people don\u2019t have a LeBron James to call up and say, \u2018Hey, I\u2019m thinking about this, what do you think about it?\u2019 That\u2019s special.\u201d What will also be special Monday night is when Wade, as has been his routine after every game this season, swaps jerseys with an opposing player; this will be the 1,001st game of Wade\u2019s dwindling NBA career. \u201cObviously this is something I wanted to do in my last year,\u201d Wade said. \u201cBut of all the players in the league, LeBron is one of my closest friends so this one will mean a little more, because of the paths that we both went down as competitors against each other and as teammates. We\u2019ll be linked together forever.\u201d And what might be said between friends and competitors caught up in that moment? Wade offers this: \u201cWe\u2019ll look at each other and say, \u2018Yo, this is it.\u2019 It\u2019s crazy that it happened so fast. We remember the night we got drafted like yesterday. But it comes fast. Just an ending of a chapter in both of our lives.\u201d * * * Shaun Powell has covered the NBA for more than 25 years. Dec. 4 \u2013 Chicago @ Indiana Last season, the Indiana Pacers were 0-7 without Victor Oladipo. This season, they\u2019re 5-4 (counting the game in which Oladipo was injured in the first quarter). Their win over the Bulls on Tuesday was pretty ugly, but for the most part, their offense has held up without its leading scorer. The Pacers have scored 106 points per 100 possessions over the nine games, a mark that\u2019s well below the league average, but down less than two points per 100 possessions from their mark in 15 games with Oladipo ( 107.9 ). Over those nine games, the Pacers have ranked second in the league in assist rate , having recorded assists on 68 percent of their buckets, up from 55 percent ( 24th ) through their 15 games with their All-Star. Their offense is less dependent on pick-and-rolls and we\u2019re seeing more action off the ball. Here are a couple of examples where they got open shots on consecutive possessions via multiple off-ball screens against the Bulls on Tuesday. On the first, Bojan Bogdanovic and Domantas Sabonis set a double pin-down screen for Doug McDermott, coming out of the left corner. Zach LaVine and Jabari Parker switch that initial screen and Parker stays with McDermott through the second screen. Then Sabonis sets another screen for Bogdanovic, who sees LaVine going under the pick and flares out to the left wing for an open three. Cory Joseph and Bogdanovic set a pair of baseline screens for McDermott, and then Joseph screens for Bogdanovic going in the opposite direction (with Sabonis ready to set another pin-down screen). LaVine switches that Joseph-Bogdanovic screen, but Justin Holiday does not, and Joseph is left all alone under the basket. One shooter on the move can create problems for a defense. Two shooters on the move is even better. Tue. Nov. 27 \u2013 Indiana @ Phoenix & Tue. His pick-and-pop game still too often results in mid-range jumpers and, though he\u2019s got a feathery touch, his 3-point shot has seemingly taken a step backward. He has shot just 21 percent on 1.5 3-point attempts per game this season, down from 36 percent on 2.4 attempts last season . But Turner still presents a threat when he rolls to the basket, and he can make good decisions with the ball. Here are a couple of examples from the last 10 days. On the first, his short roll draws a weak-side tag from Trevor Ariza and as he\u2019s catching the pocket pass from Darren Collison, he\u2019s already identifying Bogdanovic open in the corner for what was the game-winning bucket in Phoenix. On the second play, Turner sets four screens before something opens up. He catches a Tyreke Evans pass at the left elbow, draws help from Lauri Markkanen off the weak-side block, sees Ryan Arcidiacono sinking in from the weak-side corner, and gets the ball to Collison for a corner three. He turns 34 on Dec. 30 and is surrounded by teammates who asked for his autograph just a few years ago. Yet is anyone on the Los Angeles Lakers \u2014 or the NBA for that matter \u2014 showing more of a youthful giddyup right now than LeBron James? LeBron keeps defying age and the deep mileage on his body while feeding the Kia MVP conversation this season. His latest work of art was a dismantling of the San Antonio Spurs, chopping up the once-proud franchise Wednesday night. James\u2019 20 fourth-quarter points lead an exasperated Spurs coach Gregg Popovich to explain this to anyone who just parachuted in from Pluto: \u201cHave you watched LeBron James play before? He\u2019s LeBron James \u2014 that\u2019s what makes him difficult to guard.\u201d Yes, he\u2019s still LeBron James, even after two tours in Cleveland and a brief-yet-fulfilling stop in Miami. New town, team, uniform, fanboys \u2026 it doesn\u2019t matter, LeBron is building a strong case for being the best ever and, whaddya know, also making a case in the Western Conference for the fast-rising Lakers. All signs point toward a Christmas Day showdown at Golden State which might be for first place in the West. It will also be an anticipated checkpoint meeting with two players \u2013 Stephen Curry and Kevin Durant \u2013 who\u2019ve denied James championships. And speaking of which \u2026 The two-time defending champion Warriors are the latest \u201csuperteam\u201d and in Magic Johnson\u2019s and LeBron\u2019s biggest nightmare, perhaps the last for a long time. If Durant is still on the Warriors this time next season, then the grand plan put forth by the Lakers\u2019 team president and his resident superstar could fizzle out. As brilliant as LeBron looks today, he\u2019s on the clock physically and mentally. Don\u2019t ever dismiss the persistence of Father Time and the competitive patience of the player who didn\u2019t sign up for second place when he came to the Lakers. It often annoys basketball fans when the conversation jumps to the future and handicaps over who will join LeBron next season instead of staying in the present. But such is the reality in a league where free-agent shifts can shape the a franchise\u2019s direction and\/or where the Larry O\u2019Brien Trophy lands next. Durant did this three summers ago when he left Oklahoma City (and fellow star Russell Westbrook) to align himself with a more gentler and forgiving star in Curry. Suddenly, the regular season became moot and the question was: how many games the Warriors would need in each Finals before sipping champagne? Durant will once again become the focal point in free agency next summer. The most reasonable guesses point toward him signing with the Lakers, the New York Knicks or him staying put. It really doesn\u2019t matter what players or the media say between now and then, as circumstances can change. However, Durant threw grease on the fire in an interview with Bleacher Report\u2019s Ric Bucher by explaining how superstars may not be keen on playing with LeBron . Here we go again. And, you know, he\u2019s somewhat right about that. It is well documented that LeBron has never convinced another star to sign up. Sure, that\u2019s partly because it would\u2019ve meant moving to Cleveland, something Chris Bosh and Dwyane Wade either couldn\u2019t or wouldn\u2019t do. That led LeBron to take his talents to Miami. Bosh, a star previously in Toronto, wrestled constantly with the sacrifices required to be LeBron\u2019s teammate. In LeBron\u2019s second Cavs era, Kevin Love did as well. The ultimate basketball litmus test awaits LeBron as he\u2019s no longer in the snowy Midwest, and his boss is no longer Cavs owner Dan Gilbert. As we\u2019re seeing on a nightly basis, LeBron is still LeBron. (To paraphrase Popovich, good enough to position an average team for big success.) Shouldn\u2019t all that be enough to sway a Durant or another A-list free agent next summer? For now, LeBron and Magic are 0-for-1 in their attempt to debunk the theory that folks are selective when it comes to being LeBron\u2019s teammate. Last summer, Paul George chose Westbrook \u2014 a more ball-dominant star without the rings \u2014 and the Oklahoma City lifestyle over LeBron when he had the chance to jump. George didn\u2019t even give Magic the courtesy of an interview . Kyrie Irving bailed on LeBron for the Boston Celtics after they spent three seasons together and won the title in 2016 with the Cavs. While Irving\u2019s explanation for his exit seems as murky as his ( since refuted ) flat-Earth beliefs, he clearly wanted his own team to lead. In short, the \u201csuperteam\u201d trend is more myth than reality. Other than Miami and Golden State, there hasn\u2019t been a team formed specifically to win championships pronto. Superstars aren\u2019t hopping teams with regularity. Chris Paul left the LA Clippers in a trade to join James Harden on the Houston Rockets mainly because the LA Clippers weren\u2019t willing to give him a max contract. DeMarcus Cousins signed with the Warriors last summer because no other team was giving him the deal he sought . After burning bridges in San Antonio, Kawhi Leonard went to Toronto in a trade. Superstars tend to stay in place, especially if they get their money and their team is in reasonably good shape. Today\u2019s contenders were mostly built from the ground up \u2014 something that\u2019s often true in NBA lore. The Denver Nuggets, Milwaukee Bucks, Philadelphia 76ers, Sixers, Bucks and Raptors (aside from Kawhi) were all organically constructed through the Draft and trades. New Orleans Pelicans star Anthony Davis could be in play next summer if he pouts loud enough and forces a trade. Plus, he\u2019s now repped by Klutch Sports, LeBron\u2019s agency. Still, Davis hasn\u2019t sent out any trial balloons about leaving New Orleans. It\u2019s easy and reflexive to take LeBron\u2019s high level of play for granted because he\u2019s been in the clouds for his entire career. He\u2019s taking a career-high 5.9 3-pointers per game, yet still has burst and attacks the rim with the intent of posterizing foes. He remains a better rebounder, passer, scorer and clutch performer than any of his teammates. LeBron is leading a Lakers team with a young core and marginal veterans without skipping a beat or a game. They\u2019ve been helped by a soft segment of the schedule, helping the Lakers move just a few games from first in the West. It\u2019s not unreasonable to think of them as a top-three or-four team in a season where there\u2019s no clear No. 2 team behind the Warriors. Perhaps the most unselfish scorer in NBA history, his skills should give any marquee free agent reason to sign in LA, right? Maybe someone will \u2026 with the Clippers. They have a great supporting cast in place and will have millions to spend next summer on a star seeking his own team. That would be the ultimate slap in the face: Durant, Leonard or some other star decides to play in Staples Center \u2026 but not on LeBron\u2019s team. It\u2019s all worthless chatter for now. With seven months left before the crowning of the next champion, the NBA season doesn\u2019t play the free-agent game until it must. Meanwhile, LeBron is playing a tremendous game at an age when most superstars begin to develop an ache in their limbs. He\u2019s elevating the Lakers, which is a compelling argument for another great player to ride shotgun with LeBron. But suppose no one wants that seat? * * * Shaun Powell has covered the NBA for more than 25 years. You can e-mail him here , find his archive here and follow him on Twitter . (AP) \u2014 Brandon Ingram is staying home from the Los Angeles Lakers\u2019 upcoming two-game road trip due to his sprained left ankle. Ingram will have a precautionary MRI exam Thursday night. Ingram injured his ankle early in the Lakers\u2019 121-113 victory over San Antonio on Wednesday night when Spurs center LaMarcus Aldridge flagrantly fouled him. The Lakers have won 13 of their last 17 during their first season with LeBron James."},{"id":37096,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/bucks-eric-bledsoe-khris-middleton-roles","date":"2018-12-06","title":"Lasting success in Milwaukee tied to Bledsoe, Middleton (and that Giannis guy, too)","content":" * Friday on ESPN:  Warriors vs. Bucks, 9:30 ET Two old friends and coaches, their teams trending in opposite directions these days, spent some time catching up late last month when the San Antonio Spurs traveled to Milwaukee. That\u2019s where Spurs coach Gregg Popovich listened intently, perhaps a bit incredulously, as Bucks coach Mike Budenholzer talked to him again about forward Giannis Antetokounmpo. \u201cWhat was it Bud said?\u201d Popovich paused, recalling their conversation a couple days later. \u201cHe compared him to Timmy. Just in the way he leads, how he comes to work every day and how the other players see and respond to that.\u201d The lofty Tim Duncan comparison for Milwaukee\u2019s versatile, young star \u2014 so casually offered by Budenholzer, the former Spurs assistant, and so calmly affirmed by Popovich \u2014 was the headline of that particular chat. But the subtext was in their reference to \u201cthe other players,\u201d without whom Duncan\u2019s Hall of Fame-worthy tenure in San Antonio \u2014 and thus, Popovich\u2019s and Budenholzer\u2019s time there, too \u2014 might have been dramatically different.  Were it not for Manu Ginobili and Tony Parker, the two All-Star teammates with whom Duncan formed an organic and enduring threesome, the stoic master of fundamentals might have grown lonely in San Antonio. Once David Robinson clocked out, Duncan could have wound up like Anthony Davis in New Orleans or Kevin Garnett in Minnesota \u2013 a great player shouldering too much of the load. Rumors might have gained traction and, who knows, the Spurs\u2019 legendary big man might have left in mid-career for Orlando ( which nearly happened in 2000 ) or some other greener pasture. The Antetokounmpo parallel matters. \u201cThe Greek Freak\u201d is the Bucks\u2019 (and potentially the league\u2019s) MVP this season. But Khris Middleton and Eric Bledsoe arguably are Milwaukee\u2019s most important players for whatever regular season and playoff success awaits. Because without them, Antetokounmpo is just another generational talent without enough help, playing in a crowd of defenders. And \u201cwithout them\u201d is a very real possibility. Eleven seconds remained in a tie game against the Chicago Bulls when Bledsoe drove and got the ball to Brook Lopez. The veteran big man, so comfortable working from the perimeter this season, had a little trouble inside. Lopez missed a layup and two frantic taps at it. Bledsoe, at 6-foot-1, calculated quickly that the game might swing on this possession \u2014 against the Bulls! \u2014 and thrust himself upward. Reaching through the trees, he batted the ball back, out, near backcourt mate Malcolm Brogdon. The 2017 Kia Rookie of the Year thought \u201cshoot,\u201d but had a Chicago defender rushing toward him. So, Brogdon shoveled the ball to Middleton just outside the 3-point line. Middleton, Milwaukee\u2019s second-most prolific scorer, hadn\u2019t attempted a shot in nearly 16 game minutes. He was 1-for-4 in the second half, 5-for-12 overall then. No worries. Middleton\u2019s good look turned into a great moment for the Bucks, his shot from 26 feet lifting them to a 116-113 victory . Now imagine this play next November. Ball rolls aimlessly on the court at Fiserv Forum until a Chicago player picks it up. Antetokounmpo, alone on the right wing, watches helplessly. His teammates from that moment? Gone. It seems like a Bucks fan\u2019s bad dream, but four-fifths of Milwaukee\u2019s starting lineup \u2014 Middleton, Bledsoe, Lopez and Brogdon \u2014 will be free agents this summer. The finely tuned supporting cast so meticulously assembled and nurtured by general manager Jon Horst and Budenholzer could unravel seemingly overnight come July. And leave Antetokounmpo, the ultimate drive-and-kick force this season, without anyone of proven value to pass to. \u201cIt is our mission statement,\u201d Horst told NBA.com about the imperative to surround Antetokounmpo with the right supporting cast, not just one season at a time but long-term. \u201cWhat Giannis means to our team, our franchise, our city, our state kind of goes beyond words. We have to make the most of the opportunity to find and build things that fit with him.  \u201cWith \u2018Bud,\u2019 we have a style of play that fits Giannis and a coach who, in the person he is and the mentality, the passion, fits. And I think we have a great, great core group of guys that fit him. \u201cWhatever you look at doing, of course you consider talent. Of course you consider character. And there are different ways to fit guys around Giannis. But the No. 1 thing we have to consider in every decision we make \u2014 and that\u2019s what we\u2019ve done \u2014 is how does it fit the system we\u2019re playing in and the superstar we have.\u201d Secondary stars might sound like an oxymoron. But in today\u2019s NBA, it takes a constellation. Bledsoe and Middleton have been flirting with breakthroughs for some time. This season, ironically, it\u2019s their contributions toward the sum of the parts and Milwaukee\u2019s team success that might widen the spotlight enough for them to max out \u2026 and cash in. Middleton has been Antetokounmpo\u2019s wingman for all six of his freakishly skilled NBA seasons. They arrived one month apart in the summer of 2013, the skinny unknown Antetokounmpo from Greece as the 15th pick in that June\u2019s draft. In July, the quiet, small forward Middleton arrived one year removed from Texas A&M. Reluctantly, the Detroit Pistons included Middleton after his promising rookie season in the Brandon Jennings-Brandon Knight trade . Three years older than Antetokounmpo and far more ready for the NBA stage, Middleton helped initiate the younger man into the ranks, on and off the floor. Their stars finally crossed in 2016-17 \u2014 that\u2019s the season in which Antetokounmpo played in his first All-Star Game, while Middleton didn\u2019t play until February due to a severe hamstring injury . He appeared in only 29 games and misfired through a bumpy first-round loss to Toronto . The soft-spoken, 6-foot-8 native of Charleston, S.C., however, was back to his reliable, jump-shooting self last season. And this season, Middleton\u2019s adjustments to Budenholzer\u2019s game plan has led the way in Milwaukee\u2019s transformative floor-spreading. One of the league\u2019s top mid-range scorers has tamped down that aspect of his game from 36 percent of his field-goal attempts last season to 14.5 . And at the coaches\u2019 urging, instead of taking one or two dribbles inside the arc, he has been taking one or two steps back. He\u2019s on pace to shatter his personal best in 3-point attempts, projecting to 580 vs. the 407 he launched last season. His scoring and his shots are down slightly, and there are two months worth of games to go. But Middleton might have a legit chance to an All-Star berth if the Bucks\u2019 record remains gaudy enough to merit a second rep. What grabs Middleton most about the Milwaukee journey he\u2019s had? \u201cJust how much we\u2019ve grown,\u201d he said after a recent shootaround. \u201cFrom winning 14, 15 games to now becoming a championship-caliber team in six years. It takes time. \u2026 It\u2019s just a process that some guys got to go through, some guys don\u2019t. But to be on the bottom with this team and now be on the rise, it\u2019s pretty cool to see and look back on.\u201d It\u2019s rarely linear, too. Middleton\u2019s time with the Bucks has had its bumps, from his thigh injury to seeing his Pistons pal, big man Greg Monroe, wash out as a ballyhooed free-agent signing in 2015 . This week has been an odd one for Middleton, too. He got benched for the fourth quarter and overtime of the loss in New York Saturday after Budenholzer didn\u2019t like Middleton\u2019s defensive effort during a pivotal stretch. The two reportedly spoke that night, then hashed things out more completely before Monday\u2019s practice.  \u201cWe talk a lot about having high-character guys and high-IQ guys,\u201d Budenholzer told reporters, \u201cand I think that\u2019s one of the characteristics of those types of people or players that if and when something doesn\u2019t go their way, their reaction usually is to come back and fight harder, dig deeper, do more.\u201d Said Antetokounmpo: \u201cIt\u2019s not about being pissed off at your coach for keeping you out. It\u2019s about being pissed off at yourself. Khris is a really competitive guy and he wants to be there. He wants to do whatever it takes to win, and I think he was just really, really pissed at himself for letting himself down and the team down. Khris is going to come back stronger.\u201d Except that barely an hour before Milwaukee\u2019s home game Wednesday against Detroit, a 115-88 victory, Middleton was scratched as a no-show for what was termed \u201cpersonal reasons.\u201d No one was alleging any lingering resentment from the Knicks benching, but it served as a reminder of how fragile a player\u2019s game or a team\u2019s chemistry can be. And of how fleeting a season can be, too. \u201cWe all know [Giannis] needs each and every one of us,\u201d Middleton said last week. \u201cI know I need Giannis and everybody else. We\u2019ve definitely bought into each other. We know we need each other to win big and do the things we want to do.\u201d As for this summer and the possibility of a max contract offer that would end all this Milwaukee goodness, the 27-year-old said: \u201cI don\u2019t want to dive too deep into that now. I\u2019ve still got a lot to accomplish this year. If it\u2019s necessary, change has got to be made. Right now, hopefully, it doesn\u2019t get to that point.\u201d It wasn\u2019t Antetokounmpo who had to pick up Middleton\u2019s slack Wednesday night. It was Bledsoe as well, who scored a season-high 27 points in 26 minutes against the Pistons. He had 11 in the first quarter and nine in the third , enough that he could sit out the fourth. Defensively, he was the tip of the Bucks\u2019 spear that limited Detroit to 37 percent shooting. A year ago, Bledsoe \u2014 whose Twitter desperation to get out of Phoenix went viral \u2014 rolled into Milwaukee like a storm cloud. He was late to the party, having started the season with the Suns, and it wound up not being much of a party anyway at 44-38, with a coaching change from Jason Kidd to Joe Prunty halfway through. Now, Bledsoe\u2019s scoring (16 ppg) and field-goal attempts (11.7) are down, but his efficiency is up . He\u2019s shooting a career-best effective field-goal percentage of .593 and while his rebounds and assists are up from 2017-18, his turnovers down. Like Middleton, the point guard has re-aligned his offense. Approximately 40 percent of his shots have come at the rim, compared to 32 percent last season . Another 40 percent are coming from the arc, the biggest share in his nine NBA seasons. \u201cEric is just in a really good place,\u201d Budenholzer said. \u201cIt feels like he\u2019s understanding what we need in different moments. \u2026 He\u2019s attacking in transition and making big plays there. He\u2019s kind of laying it on the line and I think everybody\u2019s kind of feeding off that.\u201d Defensively, Bledsoe\u2019s mix of strength and explosiveness have hindered opposing guards as much as the Bucks\u2019 spread floor has enabled his. Budenholzer dialed that into his schemes soon after he was hired, although some of the chaos Bledsoe creates at that end is his alone. Said the coach: \u201cThere are times when I watch him and think, \u2018That\u2019s not what we told you to do. But it\u2019s kinda good.\u2019 I would say he\u2019s playing on some instinct, it looks like, defensively.\u201d  This has been the guy Milwaukee hoped it got early last season when it traded Monroe and two Draft picks for him. That Bledsoe, though, played more like a square peg trying to jam into a round hole, recklessly throwing away the ball or jogging back on defense. This one (whose wife and kids are in town with him this time around) fits. \u201cHe had a lot of bad habits he just had to let go,\u201d Middleton said. \u201cHe played the best he could for the situation. This year, he\u2019s being a lot more engaged. Knowing what we\u2019re wanting to do, knowing how we want to play, knowing how to run the [team].\u201d Said Antetokounmpo: \u201cIt\u2019s easier. Last year I was trying to figure out how Bledsoe plays, what he likes and what he does well. This year I know what he wants to do. I know when he\u2019s going to pass me the ball. I know when you\u2019ve got to give him the ball and get the hell out of his way to make a play. He\u2019s way more aggressive. And looking for his shots.\u201d Bledsoe sloughs off the praise, claiming it\u2019s simply a matter of playing hard and with great teammates. But he did admit, \u201c[I] love being here. I knew it was going to take some time for us to gel.\u201d Bledsoe\u2019s shift in stats is more likely to help him at contract time than in All-Star balloting. His game is in sync with his team\u2019s for now. Whether his business stays in sync with his employer\u2019s budget this summer remains to be seen. He too has been talked of at various points in his career as a future All-Star. Can that and any other dreams Bledsoe harbors for his NBA career be realized in Wisconsin? \u201cYeah. Yeah. We\u2019re winning,\u201d he said. \u201cI\u2019m just taking it a day at a time. Everything else will take care of itself. You take credit for wins, not for stats.\u201d The priority for a team facing such an unusual roster predicament \u2014 80 percent of its starters on expiring contracts or holding opt-outs \u2014 is to compartmentalize. For the Bucks, now is all about the games, the standings, continuous improvement (especially on defense) and where they can take it next spring. Who gets how much, and where and from whom, that\u2019s all for later. \u201cIt\u2019s like anything else,\u201d Horst said. \u201cWhen things are going well, issues don\u2019t matter. And when they\u2019re not going well, issues have to be managed.\u201d So far, contract talk and even competition hasn\u2019t reared its head within the Bucks\u2019 ranks.  \u201cThere are some personnel situations on the horizon, but no one involved would tell you those have any impact on what our focus is,\u201d Horst said. \u201cAnd that is, to have the best season we can have. I think that\u2019s what every guy, to their credit, is focused on.\u201d Between their salary commitments for 2019-20 and the cap holds to retain the rights to their own free agents, the Bucks figure to have only a small amount of space to shop for newcomers. And that\u2019s just from a payroll perspective; it doesn\u2019t address how well any new guys would plug into the system or how long it would take them to properly complement Antetokounmpo\u2019s game. Then there\u2019s the age-old challenge of convincing players, whether in-house or shopping from afar, that Milwaukee can be a viable destination.  \u201cThere are athletes where market matters,\u201d Horst said. \u201cThe excitement of an L.A. or a New York or the size of a Chicago. But I think more often than not, professional athletes want to win \u2014 I really believe that \u2014 and they like first-class everything. \u201cWhat\u2019s great about what we\u2019re building here, we\u2019re showing we can win. We\u2019ve got a superstar who\u2019s committed to this franchise. And now we\u2019ve got this ownership group that has invested in every area to make sure it\u2019s first-class. With the arena, the practice facility, the medical staff, the coaching staff. From the top down, every player who comes to this franchise is going to feel like he\u2019s being treated first-class. If we can combine that with winning and with Giannis, I think we have a chance.\u201d If ever there was an opportunity for a GM to do some gang-negotiating \u2014 getting all the Bucks\u2019 free agents and their reps in one room to hash out a hometown discount \u2014 this would seem to be it. Remember, Duncan, Ginobili and Parker often famously left millions of dollars on the table to stay together in San Antonio. Short of that, can Milwaukee keep all its assets? \u201cThe answer is, absolutely we can keep everybody,\u201d Horst said. \u201cIt\u2019s my job to understand markets and what values are, but we feel very confident that, yes, we can keep everybody if that\u2019s the direction we go. And the sale is going to be the ensemble and what the group can do.  \u201cIs there some sort of give-back or discount that\u2019s associated with that to keep us together? Maybe. But I think, really, in the scheme of where contracts are today, that\u2019s probably fairly marginal. What\u2019s really going to matter is if guys want to be here and see what this group can do together, or not.\u201d That gets back to the Spurs and the challenge of longevity, building something that sustains in an insta-contender, tear-down world. And as Popovich \u2014 who is experiencing the new way this season \u2014 said: \u201cIn this league, you don\u2019t win without talent. But to be the ultimate winner, all the other pieces have to fit around it. The best teams, guys respect each other. Feel responsible to each other. Their games are gonna change to some degree.\u201d Can that ever work again \u2026 in Milwaukee? Keep an eye on the Bucks\u2019 free agents in seven months, on Brogdon and Lopez, sure, but especially on Middleton and Bledsoe. The former could command a five-year, $190 million deal from the Bucks that, temporarily, would trounce the \u201cGreek Freak\u2019s\u201d four-year, $100 million extension signed in 2016. The latter will be seeking a raise from his current $15 million salary and, as he turns 29 Sunday, long-term security heading into his 30s. \u201cI think right now they are our \u2018Tony\u2019 and our \u2018Manu,\u2019 \u201d Horst said, playing along with the comparison. \u201cWe\u2019ve got a long ways to go before this group becomes the \u2018San Antonio Spurs,\u2019 but that\u2019s our goal, to build a team that can compete over a long period of time and win championships. \u201cI think they can become and sustain that. Both Khris and Eric are entering their prime or in their prime. They\u2019re super-high character guys. They are very talented. And they fit.\u201d * * * Steve Aschburner has written about the NBA since 1980. You can e-mail him here , find his archive here and follow him on Twitter .
