LeBron James was a ringless, 25-year-old superstar when his infamous Decision saw him jump from Cleveland to Miami in 2010. Eight straight Finals appearances, three championships and two more team changes later, the King was back in South Beach on Sunday as a nearly 34-year-old Laker. Heat fans probably felt the only difference was James\u2019 jersey. Other than that, it looked like the exact same LeBron. The devastating dunks in transition. The impossible-to-guard fadeaways. The selective and timely 3-pointers. All of it was working for James, who wound up scorching his old Florida playground for 51 points on 19-for-31 shooting. The performance was James\u2019 12th with at least 50 points, making him just the fifth player in league history to score 50-plus with three different teams. (The others: Wilt Chamberlain, Moses Malone, Bernard King and Jamal Crawford.) More importantly for the Lakers, James\u2019 effort lifted them to their fifth win in six games after a 2-5 start. Believe it or not, L.A. is now just two games out of first place in the Western Conference as the Warriors\u2019 slide continued in San Antonio. As for the Heat, Sunday was a reminder of what the franchise enjoyed for nearly half a decade: Complete dominance by the best player of his generation. Before this season began, Las Vegas had Orlando and Memphis each winning less than 35 games. Less than 20 days into November, both teams are on pace to make the over look like a good bet. The Grizzlies (10-5) logged another quality win over Minnesota with the ageless Marc Gasol pouring in 26 points and 13 rebounds. Beyond him and veteran guard Mike Conley, Memphis\u2019 biggest contributors are fourth overall pick Jaren Jackson Jr. and journeymen Garrett Temple and Shelvin Mack. And yes, that\u2019s the Grizzlies you\u2019re seeing tied for second-best in the West. Back in Florida, Orlando is making noise of its own behind a career year from soon-to-be free agent Nikola Vucevic (20.4 ppg, 10.8 rpg, 1.1 bpg, 1.1 spg, 55.6 FG%, 45.2 FG%). The Magic\u2019s win over the Knicks pushed them back above .500, a place they left for good exactly one year ago today. The Warriors have been a mess since Stephen Curry exited a Nov. 8 game against the Bucks with a groin strain, losing five of their past seven while seeing on-and-off-court drama flair up between Kevin Durant and Draymond Green. Golden State\u2019s latest setback \u2014 a 104-92 loss to the 7-7 Spurs \u2014 punctuated the team\u2019s shortcomings sans Curry: Get well soon, Steph. If he can\u2019t play, Rajon Rondo still wants to be involved. That includes taking up a coach\u2019s clipboard during in-game huddles. Unfortunately for him, he doesn\u2019t yet have leave to take full control of the coaching process. The 6-foot-1 point guard had 60 points , the ball, and a tie game on his hands with 32 seconds remaining in overtime. But the guy guarding him was Jimmy Butler, whom the Sixers acquired a week ago exactly for moments like this. Granted, Walker had already burned Butler for 60 \u2014 something the 76ers newcomer freely admitted after the game. The Hornets point guard didn\u2019t bail him out either. Walker attacked the basket \u2014 something he does better than all but five players in the league. Three things were in Butler\u2019s favor: Instead of Walker capping off the perfect storybook night, Butler rewrote its final pages. The four-time All-Star blocked Walker\u2019s layup attempt, then saved the loose ball from going out of bounds. On the opposite end, the 76ers again called on Butler. Again, he answered, punching home a dramatic left-side 3-pointer with just 0.3 seconds left. The 122-119 overtime victory was a watershed moment for the 2018-19 Sixers. Before, a near triple-double from Simmons (23 points, 11 rebounds, nine assists) and a dominant performance from Joel Embiid (33 points, 11 rebounds) might not have been enough. With Butler, not even a 60-point special could stop them. The number of times 60-plus didn\u2019t get it done over the last quarter-century: just two out of 17. Walker deserves (and will get) props regardless of the outcome. His 60 points weren\u2019t just a career-high, but a franchise best. That\u2019s significant for a team that just happens to be celebrating its 30th anniversary in the league. That may have been the best part about Walker\u2019s performance: it came with the Hornets\u2019 30th anniversary team on hand to see it. Muggsy Bogues, Alonzo Mourning, Dell Curry, Baron Davis and others watched the current face of the franchise carry the torch and ignite the crowd with it. Walker even broke out the timeless shrug patented by his team\u2019s owner. Until the final seconds, Saturday night belonged to Walker and the city of Charlotte. This dude won a million air miles after he made a layup, 3-pointer and half-court shot. To top it all off, the greatest Maverick ever gave him props! Anthony Davis scored 40-plus for the second straight game, the third time he has accomplished that feat this calendar year. Half of his production occurred at the free throw line, where he enjoyed a 20-for-21 showing. The Nuggets were hard-pressed to keep pace, as they shot just 13 free throws as a team in the 125-115 Pelicans win. One night after attempting 35 shots while registering zero assists, Donovan Mitchell proved his postgame regret was genuine. Utah\u2019s second-year guard scored 28 points (on 21 attempts) while dishing out six assists. Mitchell also added a big block on former Jazz All-Star Gordon Hayward to his timesheet. Luka Doncic was superb in Dallas\u2019 112-109 win over the defending champion Warriors. The third overall pick is playing like the pro he already was before jumping to the NBA, averaging 19.5 points, 6.6 rebounds and 4.2 assists. The Slovenian standout leads an incredibly deep and diverse rookie class in scoring. And yet here he was in mid-November, five months before the playoffs even begin, licking his chops over a regular-season matchup. For good reason: The Raptors were bringing their NBA-best 12-3 record to Boston for a potential \u2014 if ridiculously early \u2014 preview of the Eastern Conference finals. \u201cI\u2019m excited for that game,\u201d Irving said before Friday\u2019s game. \u201cObviously one game at a time, but that\u2019s just a competitor\u2019s dream to be going against the best of the best.\u201d As he\u2019s done so many times over the years, Irving rose to the occasion with one of the best games of his career, piling up season-highs of 43 points and 11 assists in a thrilling 123-116, overtime victory. Per Elias Sports, Irving is the first Celtic with 40-plus points and 10-plus assists since Antoine Walker in 2001, and third overall. ( Trivia question: What other Boston great did it? Answer below.) Anchored by Irving\u2019s ridiculous efficiency \u2014 the five-time All-Star hit 18 of 26 shots with just three turnovers \u2014 the Celtics overcame some mid-game stumbles to finish the game on a 20-9 run. It wasn\u2019t quite a full turnaround for a team that entered with the NBA\u2019s seventh-worst offensive rating. But with Jayson Tatum chipping in 21 points and Gordon Hayward hitting a handful of key free throws\/shots down the stretch, the Celtics at least looked closer to the contender most expected them to be than the 8-6 mediocrity that entered the game. \u201cIt\u2019s just great (for us) to see the growth,\u201d said Irving, a reference to last month\u2019s 12-point loss to the Raptors. \u201cTo have a great Friday night game, going against the Toronto Raptors \u2026 awesome.\u201d Given how aggressively he forced his way out of Minnesota, it shouldn\u2019t come as much of a surprise that Jimmy Butler isn\u2019t about to go quietly into the night with his new team. Playing in his first home game with the 76ers, Butler poured in 28 points, including eight in the fourth quarter, with seven assists as they held off the Jazz 113-107. Then came his postgame interview, in which he \u2026 well, just listen for yourself. Not that the Timberwolves are likely to feel too aggrieved by Butler\u2019s pot shot. They drilled the Blazers by 16 for their third straight victory since shipping him out. It took a full half for the Bucks to realize they had a game Friday. Once they did, the results couldn\u2019t have been much more impressive. Down 22 late in the second quarter and 18 at the break, the Bucks sprung to life with a monstrous 46-point third quarter , ultimately outscoring the Bulls by 37 in the second half en route to a 123-104 rout . According to ESPN\u2019s Kevin Pelton, the Bucks narrowly missed breaking the record for largest margin of victory after trailing by at least 18 points at the half. Their second-half shot chart was a masterpiece of modern basketball philosophy, with only two of their 27 buckets coming outside the paint or inside the 3-point line.  And perhaps best part of all: The Bucks didn\u2019t need Giannis Antetokounmpo to be ridiculously great to fuel the comeback. He was instead merely regular great (23 points, 13 rebounds, four assists) as Eric Bledsoe scored 25, Khris Middleton added 23 and the Bucks knocked down 18 3-pointers with 28 assists. \u201cWe knew we weren\u2019t playing hard enough,\u201d Antetokounmpo said. \u201c(Coach Mike Budenholzer) was mad. He was really upset. We don\u2019t have to have that type of half for us to pick it up. From the first minutes of the game, we have to set the tone.\u201d Said Budenholzer, \u201cA lot of credit to the guys for getting it together and playing the way we want to play.\u201d Such enthusiasm wasn\u2019t out of order after Davis managed a paltry two points in the first quarter at Smoothie King Center, at which point the Knicks led by 16. But unfortunately for Robinson and his teammates, NBA games are four quarters long. By the time they\u2019d elapsed, the Knicks were limping out of New Orleans in the face of a truly dominant performance from Davis, who recovered from his poor start to amass a season-high 43 points, 17 rebounds and five assists in a 129-124 victory . Enes Kanter summed up the onslaught as such: Jazz guard Donovan Mitchell also put up an impressive line, but of an entirely different variety. In chucking up 35 shots without a single assist, he became the first player to reach those thresholds since Carmelo Anthony in 2014, and just the fourth since the NBA-ABA merger in 1976-77. And unlike Anthony, who finished with a career-high 62 points, Mitchell converted only 13 shots en route to a relatively paltry 31. Full credit to Mitchell, though, as he at least owned up to the horror show: \u201cI took 35 shots. That can\u2019t happen. Zero assists. It\u2019s not who I am, it\u2019s not who I\u2019ve been. But so is the stuff between the highlights. Here are some things you may have missed from the last week (or so) of games\u2026 For all videos, press the SLOW-MO button at the bottom right to watch in slow motion. * * * Wed. Nov. 14 \u2013 Sixers at Magic In their first game with Jimmy Butler, the Sixers ran the first play of the first quarter for their new star. With the Magic switching the double pick-and-roll, it didn\u2019t really go anywhere, and Butler was mostly a spectator in the Sixers\u2019 offense throughout the first half. With Minnesota, Butler was in the top 20 of the league in pick-and-roll ball-handler possessions per game, but the Sixers have run the fewest pick-and-rolls in the league. No other Sixer ranks in the top 65 in pick-and-roll ball-handler possessions per game. The playbook was limited in Butler\u2019s debut, but Brett Brown will surely add some sets for Butler to do his thing as the season goes on. And down the stretch on Wednesday, the Sixers did run some pick-and-roll with Butler. It was the same set, a Butler-Joel Embiid pick-and-roll from the left side of the floor, three times in a stretch of eight possessions late the Sixers\u2019 111-106 loss to the Magic. The Sixers got three pretty good shots out of the play\u2026 The question to ask is whether it\u2019s good that Embiid is popping out to the perimeter on these pick-and-rolls instead of rolling to the basket. And if the answer to that is no, then the question to ask is if Simmons\u2019 presence on the floor (on the baseline because he can\u2019t shoot) is why Embiid is popping instead of rolling. With the score within five in the last five minutes of the fourth quarter or overtime this season, Embiid has taken 12 of his 25 shots from 3-point range and another four from mid-range. He does have a high free throw rate in the clutch, but that shot selection is less than ideal for a guy who\u2019s bigger and stronger than almost anybody else in the league. Fri. Nov. 9 \u2013 Hornets at Sixers With the Sixers up three in overtime last Friday, the Hornets ran a \u201chammer\u201d play to tie the game, and they executed it pretty well, with Malik Monk getting to the baseline, Willy Hernangomez setting a weak-side back-screen for Kemba Walker, and Walker springing free for an open corner three. But it wasn\u2019t open long enough, because Simmons was able to cover a lot of ground and get a hand on Walkers\u2019 shot to tie the game. Tue. Nov. 13 \u2013 Houston at Denver The Rockets\u2019 offense is a lot more fun to watch when the opponent doesn\u2019t switch screens. Alas, sometimes the defense has no choice. In the third quarter on Tuesday, Houston ran a fun play to create a little confusion prior to a James Harden-Clint Capela pick-and-roll along the left sideline. The first time the Rockets ran the play, the Nuggets didn\u2019t switch anything, Nikola Jokic hedged out to Harden (with Gary Harris trailing), Capela got a clean roll to the basket, and Capela got an easy dunk of a perfect pocket pass from the MVP. When the Rockets ran the same play on the very next possession, the Nuggets had Jokic on the weak side and worked out a three-way switch where Paul Millsap picked up Harden, Juancho Hernangomez covered Capela on the roll, and Harris switched onto Hernangomez\u2019s man (P.J. Tucker). Harden, of course, went to an iso. Mon. Nov. 12 \u2013 Utah at Memphis In third quarter on Monday, the Jazz set up in a pretty unique configuration, with four guys bunched together between the foul line and the 3-point arc. Then Derrick Favors ran in a circle around Donovan Mitchell to set a screen for Mitchell to flare out to the left side. It\u2019s an elaborate set-up (a semi-disguised \u201chorns\u201d set) for a Joe Ingles curl around a Rudy Gobert screen that gets a runner for Ingles, with Marc Gasol dropping back to defend Gobert\u2019s roll to the basket (with no help because the Jazz cleared out the right side of the floor). Wed. Nov. 14 \u2013 Miami at Brooklyn A team\u2019s best shooter can often be its most effective screener, because his defender has to choose between sticking with the shooter and helping on guy coming off the screen. In the third quarter of their easy win in Brooklyn on Wednesday, the Heat ran an ATO (after timeout) play with Wayne Ellington setting a back-screen at the left elbow for Tyler Johnson. Joe Harris was guarding Ellington and chose to stay attached, allowing Johnson to get an easy layup off a feed from Justise Winslow. * * * John Schuhmann is a senior stats analyst for NBA.com. "},{"id":37412,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/kia-mvp-ladder-week-3-2018-19","date":"2018-11-16","title":"Kia MVP Ladder: LeBron's climb coincides with Lakers' rise in West","content":" LeBron James doesn\u2019t just do milestones. He does milestones on the big stage about as good as anyone ever has in the NBA. And with all of the chart climbing he\u2019s done throughout his career, particularly in the past few seasons, it\u2019s no wonder he turned in the showcase effort he did Wednesday night in passing Wilt Chamberlain for fifth on the all-time scoring list, joining a fab five of all-time great scorers that starts with Kareem Abdul-Jabbar, Karl Malone, Kobe Bryant and Michael Jordan. As historic as LeBron\u2019s monstrous 44-point, 10-rebound, nine-assist effort in the win over Portland was, and with Hollywood\u2019s biggest stars either in attendance or quick to praise the city\u2019s biggest current star for yet another show-stopping performance, it also served as a reminder that he and the Lakers are clearly a threat to the order of things in the Western Conference. And that goes for both this week\u2019s Kia Race to the MVP Ladder and the Western Conference playoff chase that they were watching from the outside as recently as a week ago. LeBron moved up seven spots to second in this week\u2019s MVP Ladder, just behind Milwaukee\u2019s Giannis Antetokounmpo. (You pass Wilt Chamberlain on any career list and it has to put you in another stratosphere.) The Lakers are doing the same. They sit at 8-6 heading into Saturday\u2019s game in Orlando , the first of a three-game road swing that makes stops in both Miami (Sunday) and Cleveland (Wednesday, 8 ET on ESPN ), the only other NBA cities LeBron has called home during his career. A successful trip could provide an opportunity to make some serious noise in the standings. Despite some early hiccups that should have been expected, LeBron\u2019s obviously making himself at home with the franchise Chamberlain helped to a title before the new No. 5 on the scoring list was born. Those conversations from a few weeks ago, about what the Lakers lacked in ready-for-primetime personnel have shifted; the addition of veteran center Tyson Chandler no doubt providing a boost. All that chatter about LeBron being more interested in being a Hollywood mogul than the most dominant force in the league faded as he turned in his most efficient performance (13-of-19 from the floor and a wicked 5-fo-6 from beyond the 3-point line) of the season in that takedown of the Trail Blazers. Now the rest of the league has to be wondering: Can LeBron impose his will strongly enough and long enough to push these Lakers into the upper echelon of the Western Conference standings? If LeBron\u2019s history is any indication, the rest of the league already has its answer. * * * The top five this week in the 2018-19 Kia Race to the MVP Ladder: * * * Last week : No. 1 Season stats:  25.8 points, 12.7 rebounds, 5.6 assists, 1.4 blocks Even in defeat it\u2019s hard to look beyond Antetokounmpo\u2019s impact for the Bucks. When they suffered their first defeat at Fiserv Forum Wednesday night against the surprising Memphis Grizzlies, Antetokounmpo was once again outstanding. He shredded the Grizzlies for 31 points on an insane 10-for-14 shooting from the floor (11-for-12 from the free-throw line) to go with his nine rebounds, four assists and two blocks. His spectacular footwork and preposterous catch radius makes him a threat from outside the 3-point line and far above the rim, which makes him impossible to prepare for defensively because he stretches the floor in every way imaginable. How many players in NBA history could claim to be a legitimate threat from 3-point range while shooting as poorly (.071) as the Greek Freak has from distance this season? The Bucks have figured out the right formula in surrounding him with pieces that fit perfectly. And to his credit, Bucks coach Mike Budenholzer has adjusted his scheme to work for Antetokounmpo, rather than attempting to try it the other way around. Last week : No. 9 Season stats:  27.6 point, 7.9 rebounds, 7.2 assists, 1.5 steals A record-setting week for LeBron James, passing Wilt Chamberlain for fifth on the NBA\u2019s all-time scoring list, comes in the midst of a season-altering turn for the Lakers. Winners of four straight games, and six of their last seven, LeBron\u2019s Lakers have gone from a huge question mark to exactly where many people felt they would be in the Western Conference playoff landscape. The Lakers have earned that 8-6 overall record and have weathered plenty of drama (the fight and suspensions stemming from that Oct. 20 loss to Houston, the Magic Johnson-Luke Walton meeting fallout, etc.) as the league calendar shifts into the holiday season. This is roughly the same point in the season LeBron\u2019s first Miami Heat turned a corner. Walton has managed to get the very best from LeBron while deftly managing his minutes (33.3 in six games this month). That could be a critical move for the Lakers as this season progresses, given the finishing kick that will likely be needed to maintain playoff positioning in the deep Western Conference. Last week : No. 4 Season stats : 26.4 points, 6.2 assists, 5.2 rebounds Lillard and the Trail Blazers are not going away. So anyone expecting some drop-off from their early-season surge is wasting time looking for cracks in their foundation. The Trail Blazers were the forgotten team in the offseason, when everyone was forecasting the Utah Jazz, Denver Nuggets and others as contenders for that No. 3 spot in the Western Conference playoff chase that the Trail Blazers locked up last season. But Lillard\u2019s leadership has been stellar as he and C.J. McCollum\u2019s supporting cast has stepped up to help balance the attack. Lillard had a tough shooting night (8-for-23 from the floor) in Wednesday\u2019s loss to the Los Angeles Lakers but still almost finished with a triple-double (31 points, 11 assists and eight rebounds). It was a testament to his ability to impact a game by doing more than just scoring, which remains his most dynamic skill. Portland will need to lean on all that he brings as they continue their six-game road trip tonight at Target Center against the Minnesota Timberwolves . They finish this current swing with another statement game the day after Thanksgiving in Lillard\u2019s hometown (Oakland). Last week : No. 3 Season stats : 24.2 points, 7.8 rebounds, 3.2 assists We didn\u2019t get to see Leonard in the Raptors\u2019 previous measuring stick game, when he and Giannis Antetokounmpo both sat out of Milwaukee\u2019s Oct. 29 win over Toronto. But we\u2019ll get to see him in action tonight  (7 ET, ESPN) against a Boston Celtics team most pundits and fans alike picked as the preseason favorite in the Eastern Conference. While the Celtics are still sorting through some things with the return of their veteran All-Stars Kyrie Irving and Gordon Hayward, the Raptors continue to shine with Leonard firmly entrenched as their No. 1 option. He scored a season-high 31 points in the Raptors\u2019 Oct. 19 win over the Celtics at Air Canada Centre. The Raptors still have the same energized bench they had roughly a month ago, so they\u2019ll hit the floor at TD Garden tonight knowing exactly who and what they are and perhaps more importantly knowing exactly what they have in Leonard, who is sure to be eager to hit the floor again after a late-game turnover cost him a chance at a potential game-winning shot opportunity in Wednesday\u2019s home loss to Detroit . Last week : No. 2 Season stats : 29.5 points, 6.1 assists, 5.0 assists Curry\u2019s value to the Warriors couldn\u2019t be more obvious right now, given the tumultuous week the defending two-time champions have had without their fuel cell in uniform due to a groin injury that has cost him the past four games. He\u2019s going to miss at least three more before being evaluated again, but he\u2019s traveling with the team as they try to steady themselves after losing three of their past five games, including Thursday night\u2019s pasting from the Rockets in Houston. Before they hit the floor against the Rockets, Durant and Green vowed that they\u2019d be fine and that the pursuit of a third title would not be undone by one emotional incident.
